15.1.1.1.1 API Introduction 
Robokit provides users with the APIs related to robot operation. The entire APIs adopt the TCP request/response mode, and the 
robot as a server accepts the client's request and responds to the client. The API request consists of a header and a data area. The 
header is fixed-length, used to identify the basic information of the data packet and the length and type of the data area. The data  
area is serialized JSON data, and the corresponding JSON object can be obtained by deserializing according to the type information in 
the header. The response of the API also consists of a header and a data area. The header is a fixed-length byte obtained according 
to the request (For relationship between the response header and the corresponding request header, see below.), and the data area 
is also the serialized JSON data. 
 
API Test and Examples 
We open source API test tool on Github. The tool, Source, is written in Qt, and its source code can be used as a example. The 
compiled windows executable file can also be downloaded in Release. 
For C# example, Please click the link. 
API Category 
Types of API are divided into five, namely robot status API, robot control API, robot navigation API, robot configuration API, other 
API, and robot push API. 
1. Robot Status API : Queries various state of the robot, such as position, speed, and alarm information. 
2. Robot Control API : Sends open loop control commands to the robot, such as forward speed, rotate speed, relocating, etc. 
3. Robot Navigation API : Sends navigation commands to the robot, such as path navigation, translation and rotation. 
4. Robot Config API : Sets the parameters of the robot, as well as download and upload maps, etc. 
5. Other API : Other parameters, such as audio control, etc. 
6. Robot Push API : Uses by robot to actively push data to the currently connected client. 
Each category uses different ports, independent of each other. 
Category 
Port 
Number of Connections Allowed 
Robot Status API 
19204 
10 
Port 
The fastest time interval of API requests for each port is recommended to be 100-200ms, please do not be too fast. 
 
The robot will use the TCP KeepAlive mechanism for each established TCP connection to keep alive, and the dead connection will be 
cleared in time. 
 
Category 
Port 
Number of Connections Allowed 
Robot Control API 
19205 
5 
Robot Navigation API 
19206 
5 
Robot Configuration API 
19207 
5 
Other API 
19210 
5 
Robot Push API 
19301 
10 
If the robot receives any erroneous data packets that do not conform to the header of this protocol, it will actively close the TCP 
connection (no reply will be received). 
 
In other cases, the robot will not actively disconnect, and API users should control when the connection is interrupted. 
 
For each connection, the robot is processed in the form of request and response, that is, the next request will not be processed 
before a response is made, therefore, it is recommended that when using it, wait for the response to the previous request before 
sending the next request. 
 
 
15.1.1.1.2 API Message Structure 
The structure is as follows: 
Name 
Content 
Length (byte) 
Description 
Message 
synchronization 
header 
0x5A 
1 (uint8) 
Message synchronization header, determines the beginning of the message 
header. 
Protocol version 
1 
1 (uint8) 
The major version number of the agreement, currently 0x01 
Serial number 
 
2 (uint16) 
The serial number of the request and response (0 ~ 65535), this field of the 
request packet and the response packet is the same, and API users fill in the 
serial number by themselves. The robot's response to each request uses this 
sequence number. 
Data area length 
 
4(uint32) 
Data area length, which is the length of JSON serialized data. 
Message type (API 
number) 
 
2(uint16) 
The type of message, that is, the API number, see the API chapters in below. 
Reserved area 
 
6(uint8[6]) 
Reserved area (Do not focus on the content of the reserved area, and its content 
may not be 0 and may change.) 
Data area 
 
Depends on the 
length of the data 
area in the header. 
JSON serialized data content. 
// The C++ header structure is as follows: 
#include <stdint.h> 
struct ProtocolHeader { 
    uint8_t  m_sync; 
    uint8_t  m_version; 
    uint16_t m_number; 
    uint32_t m_length; 
    uint16_t m_type; 
    uint8_t  m_reserved[6]; 
}; 
As shown in the table above, the length of the message header is 1 + 1 + 2 + 4 + 2 + 6 = 16 bytes, and the length of the request 
and response message headers is the same. If a message type has no data area, the content of the data area length is 0x00000000. 
The message type (API number) must be one of the API numbers below. If the robot receives an undefined message type, it will 
respond with an error. If the format of the message header cannot be parsed, the robot will disconnect without any response. If 
the data area is parsed incorrectly, an error will also be responded. 
Note 1: Each request with the correct header in the message will have a response. The API number is used to correspond the 
request to the response. In general, the response API number is the request API number plus 10000 (0x2710). 
 
Note 2: The robot will not actively send data under any circumstances. 
 
Note 3: If the robot receives a message type that does not belong to a port, it will respond with an error. 
 
Note 4: The 6 bytes of the reserved area must be filled and cannot be omitted, generally filled with 0x000000000000. 
Example of Request 
Take the following request for 2002 (0x07D2) as an example: 
The structure of request data area is shown as follows： 
2002(0x07D2) is the relocation request, the parameters are x coordinate and y coordinate. The standard JSON object is as follows: 
{ 
    "x": 10.0, 
    "y": 3.0, 
    "angle": 0 
} 
In the message, it is necessary to serialize the above JSON object and stuff it into the data area of the message, and fill the length of 
the serialization into the length of the data area of the message header. 
The serialized data is {"x":10.0,"y":3.0,"angle":0}, which converts to hexadecimal as 7B 22 78 22 3A 31 30 2E 30 2C 22 79 22 3A 33 2E 
30 2C 22 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 30 7D. The length is 28(0x1c) bytes, so the header is 5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 1C 07 D2 00 00 00 00 00 00, 
and splice the header and data area together to get a request as follows (total 44 bytes): 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 1C 07 D2 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 78 22 3A 31 30 2E 30 2C 22 79 22 3A 33 2E 30 2C 22 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 30 7D 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
x 
Number 
The x coordinate in the global coordinate system, unit m 
Yes 
y 
Number 
The y coordinate in the global coordinate system, unit m 
Yes 
angle 
Number 
The angle in the global coordinate system, unit rad 
Yes 
Example of response 
Take the following response of 11004 (0x2AFC) as an example: 
The structure of response data is showmn as follows: 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
x 
Number 
The x-coordinate of the robot, unit m 
Yes 
y 
Number 
The y-coordinate of the robot, unit m 
Yes 
angle 
Number 
The angle of the robot, unit rad 
Yes 
confidence 
Number 
Location confidence of robot, range [0, 1] 
Yes 
ret_code 
Number 
API error code 
Yes 
The order of the keys in the JSON Object returned in each data area is not guaranteed, because JSON does not specify 
this. The current position of the robot is x = 6.0, y = 2.0, angle = 1.57, confidence = 0.9, represented as a JSON object as follows: 
{ 
    "ret_code": 0, 
    "x": 6.0, 
    "y": 2.0, 
    "angle": 1.57, 
    "confidence": 0.9 
} 
The serialized data is {"ret_code":0,"x":6.0,"y":2.0,"angle":1.57,"confidence":0.9}, which converts to hexadecimal as following: 
7B 22 72 65 74 5F 63 6F 64 65 22 3A 30 2C 22 78 22 3A 36 2E 30 2C 22 79 22 3A 32 2E 30 2C 
22 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 31 2E 35 37 2C 22 63 6F 6E 66 69 64 65 6E 63 65 22 3A 30 2E 39 7D 
The length is 60(0x3C) bytes, so the response header is 5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 3C 2A FC 00 00 00 00 00 00. The data after splicing is as 
follows (a total of 76 bytes): 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 3C 2A FC 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 72 65 74 5F 63 6F 64 65 22 3A 30 2C 22 78 22 3A 36 2E 30 2C 22 79 22 3A 32 2E 30 2C 
22 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 31 2E 35 37 2C 22 63 6F 6E 66 69 64 65 6E 63 65 22 3A 30 2E 39 7D 
Response Structure 
API response data area usually contains following fields: 
Field 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
ret_code 
Number 
API error code 
Yes 
create_on 
String 
API upload timestamp （added in version 3.3.3.59 or later） 
Yes 
err_msg 
String 
Error message 
Yes 
The API error code is the error code contained in the JSON object in the response data area (ret_code), which is used to indicate 
errors such as unsuccessful request execution or request error. If ret_code is 0 or default, no error occurs; if not 0, an error has 
occurred. For details, see error code in Appendix A: API error code. When there is no error, err_msg will also be defaulted, that is, 
the data area will be empty. create_on is the timestamp when the API returns, added in version 3.3.3.59. 
15.1.1.1.3 Coordinate System 
In Robokit, there are two sets of coordinate systems, namely the global coordinate system and the robot coordinate system. The 
global coordinate system is the right-handed coordinate system, that is, the coordinate system of the map and the operations 
related to the map and the location all use the global coordinate system. For example, the position of the robot (x, y, r) describes 
the x coordinate, y coordinate, and r angle of the robot in the global coordinate system. Schematic diagram see below. 
For the movement of the robot itself, you need to refer to the robot coordinate system. The robot coordinate system is the right-
hand coordinate system. Fordetails, see below. 
Global Coordinate System 
The global coordinate system is the right-handed coordinate system. 
Origin of Global Coordinate System 
Open a map in Roboshop to see the origin of the global coordinate system of the map. You can also change the position of the 
origin in the map arbitrarily through the coordinate transformation tool. 
 
Robot Coordinate System 
The robot coordinate system is the right-handed coordinate system. 
Origin of Robot Coordinate System 
For a robot moving in a differential manner, the origin of the robot coordinate system is the center point of the wheelbase of the 
two wheels, as shown in the following figure: 
 
Note: When we talk about the speed of the robot, in general, vx is the speed of the robot in the x-axis direction of the robot 
coordinate system, vy is the speed of the robot in the y-axis direction of the robot coordinate system, and w is the angular velocity 
of the robot in robot coordinate system. 
 
15.1.1.1.4 API Usage Precautions 
1. International units are used, such as m, rad, m/s, etc, except those of some specified values. 
2. The API number of response is the API number of request + 10000 (0x2710), and the request corresponds to the 
response respectively. 
3. Avoid sending any non-ACSII characters, especially operations related to map names, because map names containing 
Chinese characters will be considered illegal. 
4. The order of the keys in the JSON Object returned in each data area is not guaranteed, because JSON does not specify 
this. 
5. If there is a key-value in the JSON Object which is not mentioned in the API response data area, you can ignore it 
directly. 
 
 
15.1.1.2 API User Guide 
This guide introduces the use of this TCP API protocol to control the robot for continuous path navigation (This is the most 
common way.). 
Path Navigation Process 
1. Start the Robot 
2. Wait for the robot to boot complete (After the robot is successfully connected using TCP, the boot is completed.) 
3. Perform relocation 2002 
4. Query location status and wait for relocating completion 1021 
5. Confirm correct location 2003 
6. Perform path navigation 3051 
7. Query navigation status and wait for navigation to complete 1020 
8. Repeat steps 6 and 7 to achieve continuous path navigation 
If the location was correct and did not move after the robot was turned off the last time, then step 3 can be omitted after the robot 
is turned on. After querying that the relocating is completed, directly confirm that the location is correct. 
Robot Status API 
The robot status API is used to query all status of the robot.

15.1.1.3.6 Robot Blocked Status Inquiry 
Request 
• 
API number: 1006 (0x03EE) 
• 
Name: robot_status_block_req 
• 
Description: Robot blocked status inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: None 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 03 EF 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
• 
API number: 11006 (0x2AFE) 
• 
Name: robot_status_block_res 
• 
Description: Response of robot blocked status inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
If there is a key-value in the JSON Object which is not mentioned in the API response data area, you can ignore it directly, which 
also applies for the following content. 
 
 
 
 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
blocked 
boolean 
Whether the robot is blocked 
YES 
block_reason 
number 
Reasons for being blocked, 0 = Ultrasonic, 1 = Laser, 2 = Fallingdown, 3 = Collision, 4 = 
Infrared, 5 = Lock, 6 = dynamic obstacle, 7 = virtual laser, 8 = 3D camera 
YES 
block_x 
number 
The x coordinate of the nearest obstacle(world coordinate system), unit: m 
YES 
block_y 
number 
The y coordinate of the nearest obstacle(world coordinate system), unit: m 
YES 
block_ultrasonic_id 
number 
The blocked ultrasonic id number, only makes sense when block_reason = 0, 
It is abandoned by 3.2.8.0, and changes to block_id. 
YES 
block_di 
number 
The ID number of the blocked DI, only makes sense when block_reason = 2, 3, 4 
It is abandoned by 3.2.8.0, and changes to block_id. 
YES 
block_id 
number 
The blocked ID, only makes sense when the block_reason = 0、2、3、4、9、10 
It is added from 3.2.8.0. 
是 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
slowed 
boolean 
Whether the robot slows down. 
YES 
slow_reason 
number 
Reasons for slowing down, 0 = Ultrasonic, 1 = Laser, 2 = Fallingdown, 3 = Collision, 4 = 
Infrared, 5 = Lock, 6 = dynamic obstacle, 7 = virtual laser, 8 = 3D camera 
YES 
slow_x 
number 
The x coordinate of nearest obstacle that caused the slow down, unit: m 
YES 
slow_y 
number 
The y coordinate of nearest obstacle that caused the slow down, unit: m 
YES 
slow_ultrasonic_id 
number 
Ultrasonic id number which caused slow down, only makes sense when slow_reason = 0 
It is abandoned by 3.2.8.0, and changes to block_id. 
YES 
slow_di 
number 
The id number of the DI which caused slow down, only makes sense when slow_reason = 2, 3, 
4 
It is abandoned by 3.2.8.0, and changes to block_id. 
YES 
slow_id 
number 
The slowed ID, only makes sense when slow_reason = 0、2、3、4、9、10. 
It is added from 3.2.8.0. 
是 
Response Example 
{ 
  "block_x": 15.2845, 
  "block_y": -8.1834, 
  "blocked": false, 
  "ret_code": 0, 
  "slowed": false 
}

15.1.1.3.10 Robot Path Status Inquiry 
Request 
• 
API number: 1010 (0x03F2) 
• 
Name: robot_status_path_req 
• 
Description: Robot path status inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: None 
Note: The path data of the robot is meaningful only during free navigation. The robot moves along the drawn Bezier curve 
during path navigation. The path data queried through this API is meaningless when the robot moves during path navigation. If you 
need to query the path data during path navigation, please refer to 1020 Navigation status. 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 03 F2 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
•

Name

Response Example 
The following is the data of five path points: 
{ 
    "path": [[1.0, 1.2], [2.0, 1.3], [3.2, 2.1], [3.4, 1.4], [3.9, 1.5]] 
} 
The above path consists of 5 points, and the 5 points are (1.0, 1.2), (2.0, 1.3), (3.2, 2.1), (3.4, 1.4), (3.9, 1.5), which represent the 
five coordinates in the world coordinate system. Connecting these 5 points in sequence is the current planned path of the robot.

object form is as follows: 
{ 
    "id": 0,      // ultrasonic node ID 
    "dist": 0.2,  // the distance that the ultrasonic detected(Unit:m) 
    "valid": true // valid or not 
} 
After obtaining id and dist, it needs to be converted into values in the world coordinate system according to the corresponding 
ultrasound configuration in the model file. 
Response Example

      "valid": false 
    },

      "valid": true 
    },

      "id": 4, 
      "dist": 0.03, 
      "valid": false 
    } 
  ] 
} 
For the ease of reading, the JSON data here is in an expanded form. In practice, the JSON data area is compact in order to reduce 
the data flow, and there will be no extra spaces and line breaks. The same applies to the following text. 
 
 
15.1.1.3.17 Robot PGV Data Inquiry 
Note：PGV means Position Guided Vision. 
Request 
•

• 
Name: robot_status_pgv_req 
• 
Description: Robot PGV data inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: None

5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 03 F9 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
• 
API number: 11017 (0x2B09) 
• 
Name: robot_status_pgv_res 
•

• 
JSON data area: See table below 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
pgvs 
array[object] 
QR code identification data, see below for data examples 
YES 
ret_code 
number 
API error code 
YES 
create_on 
string 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
string 
Error message 
YES 
The format of object is as follows: Mainly focusing on device_address (id of PGV device) and tag_value (data of QR code tag) 
{ 
    // id of PGV device 
    "device_address": 1, 
    "error_code": 0, 
    "header": { 
        "data_nsec": "1750000088331", 
        "frame_id": "", 
    "pub_nsec": "0", 
    "seq": "0" 
    }, 
    "is_DMT_detected": true, 
    "is_absolute_X_pos_valid": true, 
    "pgv_info": { 
        "func": 1, 
        "r": 0, 
        "x": 0, 
        "y": 0, 
        "z": 0 
    }, 
    "tag_diff_angle": 1744, 
    "tag_diff_x": 256, 
    "tag_diff_y": 47, 
    // data of QR code tag 
    "tag_value": 1, 
    "warning_code": 0 
} 
Response Example 
The data for the two PGV devices is as follows: 
{ 
  "pgvs": [ 
    { 
      "device_address": 0, 
      "error_code": 0,

        "data_nsec": "1749997924588", 
        "frame_id": "", 
        "pub_nsec": "0", 
        "seq": "0" 
      }, 
      "is_DMT_detected": false, 
      "is_absolute_X_pos_valid": false,

        "func": 1, 
        "r": 0, 
        "x": 0, 
        "y": 0, 
        "z": 0 
      }, 
      "tag_diff_angle": 0, 
      "tag_diff_x": 0, 
      "tag_diff_y": 0, 
      "tag_value": 0, 
      "warning_code": 0 
    }, 
    { 
      "device_address": 1, 
      "error_code": 0, 
      "header": { 
        "data_nsec": "1749997924588", 
        "frame_id": "", 
        "pub_nsec": "0", 
        "seq": "0" 
      }, 
      "is_DMT_detected": true,

15.1.1.3.19 Robot Navigation Status Inquiry 
Request 
• 
API number: 1020 (0x03FC) 
• 
Name: robot_status_task_req 
• 
Description: Robot navigation status inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
simple 
boolean 
Whether to return only simple data, true = yes, false = no, and the default is no. 
YES 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 03 FC 00 00 00 00 00 00 
// Only return simple data 
// {"simple":true} 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 0F 03 FC 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 73 69 6D 70 6C 65 22 3A 74 72 75 65 7D 
Response 
• 
API number: 11020 (0x2B0C) 
• 
Name: robot_status_task_req 
• 
Description: Response of robot navigation status inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
If there is a key-value in the JSON Object which is not mentioned in the API response data area, you can ignore it directly, which 
also applies for the following content. 
 
If only simple data is returned, only task_status in the fields in the table below. 
 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
task_status 
number 
0 = NONE, 1 = WAITING(This state is currently impossible), 2 = RUNNING, 3 = 
SUSPENDED, 4 = COMPLETED, 5 = FAILED, and 6 = CANCELED. 
YES 
task_type 
number 
navigation type, 0 = no navigation, 1 = free navigation to a coordinate, 2 = free navigation 
to a station, 3 = path navigation to a station, 7 = translational/rotation, and100 = other. 
YES 
target_id 
string 
The current navigation target, this field is valid only when task_type is 2 or 3, when 
task_status is RUNNING, it means that robot are going to this station, when task_status is 
COMPLETED, it means that robot have reached this station, when task_status is FAILED, it 
means that robot have failed to go to this station, if task_status is SUSPENDED, then 
navigation to this station is paused. 
YES 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
target_point 
array[number] 
The current navigation coordinate. It is an array including 3 numbers, coordinate of X, 
Y,and R in world coordinate respectively. This field is valid only when task_type is 1, and 
when task_status is RUNNING, robot are going to this station; when task_status is 
COMPLETED, robot have reached this station; when task_status is FAILED, robot have failed 
to go to this station; when task_status is SUSPENDED, navigation to this station is paused. 
YES 
finished_path 
array[string] 
The stations that have passed on the current navigation path, it is an array of stations. 
This field is valid only when task_type is 3 or 4. It will list all the intermediate stations that 
have passed. 
YES 
unfinished_path 
array[string] 
The stations that have not passed on the current navigation path,it is an array of stations. 
This field is valid only when task_type is 3 or 4. It will list all the intermediate stations that 
have not been passed. 
YES 
move_status_info 
string 
Additional information about navigation tasks 
YES 
ret_code 
number 
API error code 
YES 
create_on 
string 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
err_msg 
string 
error message 
YES 
Response Example 
The following data indicates that the robot is using path navigation to go to the station with the id "LM6", the stations that have 
passed are LM1, LM2, LM3, and the stations that have not passed are LM4, LM5, LM6 
{ 
  "task_status": 2, 
  "task_type": 3, 
  "target_id": "LM1", 
  "finished_path": [ 
    "LM1", 
    "LM2", 
    "LM3" 
  ], 
  "unfinished_path": [ 
    "LM4", 
    "LM5", 
    "LM6" 
  ] 
} 
If only simple data is returned (there are only 17 characters in the data area): 
{"task_status":4} 
 
 
15.1.1.3.20 Robot Task Status Package Inquiry

5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 03 FD 00 00 00 00 00 00

• 
API number: 11021 (0x2B0D) 
• 
Name: robot_status_reloc_res 
• 
Description: Response of robot localization status inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
If there is a key-value in the JSON Object which is not mentioned in the API response data area, you can ignore it directly, which 
also applies for the following content. 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
reloc_status 
number 
0 = FAILED(Localization failed), 1 = SUCCESS(Localization is correct), 2 = RELOCING(Relocating),

YES

number 
API error code 
YES

string 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
string 
Error message 
YES 
Note: The localization status (1021) is used to indicate whether the current robot localization status is correct. If the localization 
status is COMPLETED, the relocation has been completed, but the user has not confirmed. In this case, you need to confirm (2003) 
or relocate. After the user confirms that the localization is correct, the localization status will change to SUCCESS. 
Response Example 
{ 
  "reloc_status": 1 
}

number

15.1.1.3.26 Robot Roller Status Inquiry 
Only makes sense for robots equipped with rollers or belts.

•

•

• 
JSON data area: None 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 04 05 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
• 
API number: 11029 (0x2B15) 
• 
Name: robot_status_roller_res 
• 
Description: Response of robot roller status inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
roller_mode 
boolean 
Operating mode, false = manual, true = automatic 
YES 
roller_state 
number 
Running status, 0x01 = standby, 0x02 = executing, 0x03 = executing completed, 0xFF = 
executing failed 
YES 
roller_enable 
boolean 
Whether the roller is enabled, false = disabled, true = enabled 
YES 
roller_error_code 
number 
Roller error code 
YES 
roller_isFull 
boolean 
Whether the roller has goods, false = no goods, true = has goods 
YES 
roller_speed 
number 
Motor speed of roller 
YES 
roller_emc 
boolean 
Whether the roller in Estop, false = not Estop, true = Estop 
YES 
peripheral_data 
array[number] 
User-defined data in a peripheral 
YES 
ret_code 
number 
API error code 
YES 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
create_on 
string 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
string 
Eerror message 
YES 
roller_error_code Definition: 
0x00（00）,       // No error 
0x11（17）,       // Motor error 
0x01（01）,       // Roller has goods（Load） 
0x02（02）,       // Roller is empty（Unload） 
0x03（03）,       // Load timeout 
0x04（04）,       // Unload timeout 
0x05（05）,       // The goods are too long 
Response Example 
{ 
  "peripheral_data": [], 
  "ret_code": 0,

  "roller_enable": false,

  "roller_isFull": false, 
  "roller_mode": false, 
  "roller_speed": 0, 
  "roller_state": 0 
}

15.1.1.3.28 Robot Alarm Status Inquiry 
Request 
•

•

•

•

Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 04 1A 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
• 
API number: 11050 (0x2B2A) 
• 
Name: robot_status_alarm_res 
• 
Description: Query the response of the current alarm state of the robot. 
• 
JSON data area: See the table below. 
 
 
 
 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
fatals 
Array[Object] 
Fatal alarm array, all Fatal alarms will appear in the data, see the object format below. 
Yes 
errors 
Array[Object] 
Error alarm array, all Error alarms will appear in the data, see the object format below. 
Yes 
warnings 
Array[Object] 
Warning alarm array, all Warning alarm will appear in the data, the object format is described 
below. 
Yes 
notices 
Array[Object] 
Notice alarm array, all Warning alarm will appear in the data, the object format is described 
below. 
Yes 
ret_code 
Number 
API error code 
Yes 
create_on 
String 
API upload timestamp 
Yes 
err_msg 
String 
Error message 
Yes 
The object format is as follows: 
{"50000":1497698400,"desc":"xxxxx","times":1}  
// Key is the alarm code. The corresponding value is the number of seconds from Thu Jan 01 08:00:00 1970 to the time when 
the alarm code is generated, desc is the English description corresponding to the error code, and times is the number of 
times. 
Response Example 
{ 
  "fatals": [ 
    { 
      "50000": 1497698400, 
      "desc": "xxxxx", 
      "times": 1 
    } 
  ], 
  "errors": [ 
    { 
      "52201": 1497698402, 
      "desc": "xxxxx", 
      "times": 1 
    }, 
    { 
      "52118": 1497698404, 
      "desc": "xxxxx", 
      "times": 1 
    } 
  ], 
  "warnings": [ 
    { 
      "54003": 1497698405, 
      "desc": "xxxxx", 
      "times": 1 
    } 
  ], 
  "notices": [ 
    { 
      "56000": 1497698505, 
      "desc": "xxxxx", 
      "times": 20 
    } 
  ] 
} 
 
 
15.1.1.3.29 Batch Data Inquiry 1 
Request 
• 
API number: 1100 (0x044C) 
• 
Name: robot_status_all1_req 
• 
Description: Batch data inquiry 1 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
All1 is to get most of the previously mentioned status data in one request, 
including 1000, 1001, 1002, 1003, 1004, 1005, 1006, 1007, 1008, 1009, 1010, 1011, 1012, 1013, 1014, 1015, 1016, 1017, 1019, 1020, 1021, 1022, 1025, 1027, 
1028, 1029, 1030, 1050, etc 
 
 
 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
keys 
array[string] 
Only return the specified key-value in the array, and the default is to return all data. 
YES 
return_laser 
boolean 
Whether to return the laser data (the data of 1009), true = return, false = not return, and 
the default is return. 
YES 
return_beams3D 
boolean 
Whether to return the multi-beam 3D laser data (the data of 1009), true = return, false = 
not return, and the default is false. 
NO 
Request Example 
// Return all data. 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 04 4C 00 00 00 00 00 00 
// Return only the inquired data. 
{"keys":["last_station","current_map"],"return_laser":false,"return_beams3D":false} 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 53 04 4C 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 6B 65 79 73 22 3A 5B 22 6C 61 73 74 5F 73 
74 61 74 69 6F 6E 22 2C 22 63 75 72 72 65 6E 74 
5F 6D 61 70 22 5D 2C 22 72 65 74 75 72 6E 5F 6C 
61 73 65 72 22 3A 66 61 6C 73 65 2C 22 72 65 74 
75 72 6E 5F 62 65 61 6D 73 33 44 22 3A 66 61 6C 
73 65 7D

•

also applies for the following content.

of 11000, 11001, 11002, 11003, 11004, 11005, 11006, 11007, 11008, 11009, 11010, 11011, 11012, 11013, 11014, 11015, 11016, 11017, 11019, 11020, 11021, 11

15.1.1.3.30 Batch Data Inquiry 2 
Request 
• 
API number: 1101 (0x044D) 
• 
Name: robot_status_all2_req 
• 
Description: Batch data inquiry 2 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
All2 is to get much frequently updated data (such as location, speed, etc.) in one request, 
including 1004, 1005, 1006, 1009, 1010, 1011, 1012, 1013, 1014, 1016, 1017, 1020, 1050 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
return_laser 
boolean 
Whether to return the laser data (the data of 1009), true = return, false = not return, and the default 
is return. 
YES 
Request Example 
// Return all data. 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 04 4D 00 00 00 00 00 00 
// Don't return laser data. 
{"return_laser":false} 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 16 04 4D 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 72 65 74 75 72 6E 5F 6C 61 73 65 72 22 3A  
66 61 6C 73 65 7D 
Response 
• 
API number: 11101 (0x2B5D) 
• 
Name: robot_status_all2_res 
• 
Description: Response of batch data inquiry 2 
• 
JSON data area: See table below 
If there is a key-value in the JSON Object which is not mentioned in the API response data area, you can ignore it directly, which 
also applies for the following content. 
 
The JSON data area will contain all key-values 
of 11004, 11005, 11006, 11008, 11009, 11010, 11011, 11012, 11013, 11014, 11016, 11017, 11020, 11050 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
mode 
number 
Robot running status, manual=0, and automatic =1 
YES 
x 
number 
The x coordinate of the robot, unit: m 
YES 
y 
number 
The x coordinate of the robot, unit: m 
YES 
angle 
number 
The angle coordinate of the robo, unit: rad 
YES 
confidence 
number 
Confidence of robot's localization, range [0, 1] 
YES 
current_station 
string 
The id of the station where the robot is currently located(this 
judgment is strict, the robot must be very close to a certain 
station(<50cm), otherwise it is a null character, that is, it is not at 
any station) 
YES 
last_station 
string 
id of the previous station where the robot is located 
YES 
vx 
number 
The actual speed of the robot in the x direction of the robot 
YES 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
coordinate system, unit: m/s 
vy 
number 
The actual speed of the robot in the y direction of the robot 
coordinate system, unit: m/s 
YES 
w 
number 
The actual angular velocity of the robot in the robot coordinate 
system (i.e., turn clockwise to negative and counterclockwise to 
positive), unit: rad/s 
YES

number 
Single steering wheel robot's current steering wheel angle, unit: rad 
YES 
spin 
number

YES

number 
The speed the robot receives in the x direction of the robot 
coordinate system, unit: m/s 
YES

number 
The speed the robot receives in the y direction of the robot 
coordinate system, unit: m/s 
YES 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
r_w 
number

positive), unit: rad/s 
YES 
r_steer 
number 
The steering wheel angle received by the single steering wheel 
robot, unit: rad 
YES

number 
The rotation speed of the tray(if exists) received by robot, unit: rad/s 
YES 
steer_angles 
array[number] 
The current steer wheel angle of a multi-steering wheel robot, 
double-steering wheel robot = [front steering wheel angle, rear 
steering wheel angle], unit: rad 
YES

array[number] 
The steer wheel angle received by the multi-steer wheel robot, 
double-teering wheel robot = [front steering wheel angle, rear 
steering wheel angle], unit: rad 
YES

boolean 
Whether the robot chassis is stationary (walking motor) 
YES

Type 
Description

Default

obstacle, 7 = virtual laser, 8 = 3D camera 
YES

number

YES

The y coordinate of the nearest obstacle(world coordinate system), 
unit: m

Type

Sequential waypoint data, sequential connection is the robot

array[string] 
An array of ids for the regions where the robot is located (Since

region at a time.). The array may be empty. 
YES 
emergency 
boolean 
true means the emergency stop button is activated (pressed), false

YES

  false = low level

  true = enabled 
  false = disabled

  false = low level

number 
0 = NONE, 1 = WAITING(This state is currently impossible), 2 =

CANCELED 
YES 
task_type 
number 
navigation type, 0 = no navigation, 1 = free navigation to a 
coordinate, 2 = free navigation to a station, 3 = path navigation to 
YES 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
a station, 7 = translational/rotation, 100 = other 
target_id 
string 
The current navigation target, this field is valid only when task_type 
is 2 or 3, when task_status is RUNNING, it means that robot are 
going to this station, when task_status is COMPLETED, it means that 
robot have reached this station, when task_status is FAILED, it means 
that robot have failed to go to this station, if task_status is 
SUSPENDED, then navigation to this station is paused 
YES 
target_point 
array[number] 
The current navigation coordinate. It is an array including 3 
numbers, coordinate of X, Y,and R in world coordinate respectively. 
This field is valid only when task_type is 1, and when task_status is 
RUNNING, robot are going to this station; when task_status is 
COMPLETED, robot have reached this station; when task_status is 
FAILED, robot have failed to go to this station; when task_status is 
SUSPENDED, navigation to this station is paused. 
YES 
finished_path 
array[string] 
The stations that have passed on the current navigation path, it is 
an array of stations. This field is valid only when task_type is 3 or 4. 
YES 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
It will list all the intermediate stations that have passed 
unfinished_path 
array[string] 
The stations that have not passed on the current navigation path,it 
is an array of stations. This field is valid only when task_type is 3 or 
4. It will list all the intermediate stations that have not been passed 
YES 
fatals 
array[object] 
Array of Fatal alarm, all Fatal alarms will appear in the array 
YES 
errors 
array[object] 
Array of Error alarm, all Error alarms will appear in the array 
YES 
warnings 
array[object] 
Array of Warning alarm, all Warning alarms will appear in the array 
YES 
notices 
array[object] 
Array of Notice, all Notice will appear in the array 
YES 
ret_code 
number 
API error code 
YES 
create_on 
string 
API upload timestamp 
YES

•

•

•

// Return all data.

•

•

•

also applies for the following content. 
 
The JSON data area will contain all key-values of 11002, 11007, 11021, 11022, 11025

}

15.1.1.3.34 Status Station Information of Current Map Inquiry 
This API is used to get the coordinates, angles and type information of all the station in the map. 
Request 
• 
API number: 1301 (0x0515) 
• 
Name: robot_status_station_req 
• 
Description: Station information of currently loaded map inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: None 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 05 15 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
• 
API number: 11301 (0x2C25) 
• 
Name: robot_status_station_res 
• 
Description: Response of station information of currently loaded map inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
stations 
array[object] 
station array, if there are no stations in the map, it will be an empty array, see object form 
below 
YES 
ret_code 
number 
API error code 
YES 
create_on 
string 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
string 
Eerror message 
YES 
The form of object in the following: 
{ 
    "id": "LM1",        // station id 
    "type": "LocationMark", // Station type: LocationMark, ChargePoint ... 
    "x": 1.23,          // The x coordinate (m) of the station in the world coordinate system 
    "y": 4.56,          // The y coordinate (m) of the station in the world coordinate system 
    "r": 1.57,          // The orientation angle (rad) of the station in the world coordinate system 
    "desc": "xxxxx"     // Remarks of the station, if it is Chinese, it is Unicode encoding, such as: \u5907\u6ce8 
} 
Response Example 
{ 
  "stations": [ 
    { 
      "id": "LM1", 
      "type": "LocationMark", 
      "x": 1.23, 
      "y": 4.56, 
      "r": 1.57, 
      "desc": "xxxxx" 
    }, 
    { 
      "id": "LM2", 
      "type": "LocationMark", 
      "x": -1.23, 
      "y": 4.56, 
      "r": 3.14, 
      "desc": "" 
    }, 
    { 
      "id": "CP1", 
      "type": "ChargePoint", 
      "x": -1.23, 
      "y": -4.56, 
      "r": 0, 
      "desc": "" 
    } 
  ], 
  "ret_code": 0 
} 
 
 
15.1.1.3.36 Robot Parameters Inquiry 
Request 
• 
API number: 1400 (0x0578) 
• 
Name: robot_status_params_req 
• 
Description: Robot parameters inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
plugin 
string 
The name of the plug-in. If it defaults (empty), it indicates to inquire all the parameters of all plug-ins. 
YES 
param 
string 
Parameter name. If plugin exists, but param defaults (empty), it means to inquire all the parameters of 
the plugin. Otherwise it is to inquire the specified parameters of the plugin. 
YES 
Data Example: 
Inquiring the MaxAcc parameter of the MoveFactory plug-in is shown in the following. 
{ 
    "plugin": "MoveFactory", 
    "param": "MaxAcc" 
} 
Request Example 
Omitted 
Response 
• 
API number: 11400 (0x2C88) 
• 
Name: robot_status_params_res 
• 
Description: Response of robot parameters inquiry 
• 
JSON data area: see below. 
A: If both plugin and param in the request are not default, it means to query a parameter of a specific plug-in. Let's take the 
MoveFactory plugin as an example to illustrate the format of the data area. 
plugin = "MoveFactory", param = "MaxAcc", the response data area of inquiring the MaxAcc parameter of the MoveFactory plug-in 
is as follows: 
{ 
    "MoveFactory": {  
    // Only when the query is successful, the plug-in does not exist, the parameter does not exist or other errors occur, 
please see ret_code 
        "MaxAcc": { 
            "value": 0.5,    // The value field indicates its value, and the value type varies with the parameter. For the 
value type of each parameter, refer to Appendix 3 
            "defaultValue": 0.5,   // default value 
            "minValue": 0.0,       // minimum value 
            "maxValue": 10.0,      // maximum value 
            "desc": "maximum acceleration",   // description 
            "group": "Navigation", // group 
            "advanced": false,     // advanced parameters 
            "type": "double"       // parameter's type 
        } 
    }, 
    "ret_core": 0, // default 
    "err_msg": ""  // default 
} 
B: If plugin is not default but param is default in the request, it means to query all the parameters of a specific plugin. Let's take 
NetProtocol plugin as an example to illustrate the format of the data area. 
plugin = "NetProtocol", param default or param="", querying all parameters of the NetProtocol plugin is shown as follows: 
{ 
    "NetProtocol": { 
    // Only when the query is successful, the plug-in does not exist or other errors occur, please see ret_code 
        // suppose NetProtocol has two parameters: defaultAutoMode, ControlMotionDuration 
        "defaultAutoMode": { 
            "value": false, 
            "defaultValue": false, 
            "desc": "The default mode is automatic after start", 
            "group": "Network", 
            "advanced": false, 
            "type": "bool" 
        }, 
        "ControlMotionDuration": { 
            "value": 500, 
            "defaultValue": 500, 
            "minValue": 0, 
            "maxValue": 5000, 
            "desc": "The duration of open-loop motion command delivery speed(ms)", 
            "group": "Network", 
            "advanced": true, 
            "type": "uint32" 
        } 
    }, 
    "ret_core": 0, // default 
    "err_msg": ""  // default 
} 
C: If plugin is default in the request, it means query all parameters. 
plugin default or plugin="", query all parameters: 
{ 
    // If there is no error, all plug-ins and all the parameters included in their runtime will be listed in the 
following form. This is just an example. There will be many plug-ins and parameters in actual runtime. Please refer to 
Appendix 3 for specific plug-in and parameter descriptions. 
    "NetProtocol": { 
        "defaultAutoMode": { 
            "value": false, 
            "defaultValue": false, 
            "desc": "The default mode is automatic after start", 
            "group": "Network", 
            "advanced": false, 
            "type": "bool" 
        }, 
       "ControlMotionDuration": { 
            "value": 500, 
            "defaultValue": 500, 
            "minValue": 0, 
            "maxValue": 5000, 
            "desc": "Duration of open-loop motion command delivery speed(ms)", 
            "group": "Network", 
            "advanced": true, 
            "type": "uint32" 
        } 
    }, 
    "MoveFactory": { 
        "MaxAcc": { 
            "value": 0.5, 
            "defaultValue": 0.5, 
            "minValue": 0.0, 
            "maxValue": 10.0, 
            "desc": "maximum acceleration", 
            "group": "Navigation", 
            "advanced": false, 
            "type": "double" 
        }, 
        "MaxSpeed": { 
            "value": 0.3, 
            "defaultValue": 0.5, 
            "minValue": 0.0, 
            "maxValue": 10.0, 
            "desc": "maximum speed", 
            "group": "Navigation", 
            "advanced": false, 
            "type": "double" 
        }, 
        "MaxRotAcc": { 
            "value": 60, 
            "defaultValue": 60, 
            "minValue": 0.0, 
            "maxValue": 360.0, 
            "desc": "maximum  angular acceleration", 
            "group": "Navigation", 
            "advanced": false, 
            "type": "double" 
        }, 
        "MaxRotSpeed": { 
            "value": 90, 
            "defaultValue": 60, 
            "minValue": 0.0, 
            "maxValue": 360.0, 
            "desc": "maximum angular velocity", 
            "group": "Navigation", 
            "advanced": false, 
            "type": "double" 
        } 
        // ... 
    }, 
    // .... 
    "ret_core": 0, // default 
    "err_msg": ""  // default 
} 
Response example

  "NetProtocol": { 
    "ArmIP": { 
      "advanced": true, 
      "defaultValue": "192.168.192.200", 
      "desc": "IP address of the robot arm", 
      "group": "Network", 
      "type": "string", 
      "value": "192.168.192.200" 
    },

      "advanced": false,

15.1.1.4 Robot Control API 
The robot control API is mainly used to send open-loop control commands. 
Note: Confirm location correct(2003) can only be used when Robot map loading status(1022) is SUCCESS, and Robot map loading 
status(1021) is COMPLETED. After confirming correct location, Robot location status(1021) will become SUCCESS. 
 
15.1.1.4.1 API list 
Request 
Serial Number 
Name 
Description 
2000 
robot_control_stop_req 
Stop open loop 
2002 
robot_control_reloc_req 
Relocation 
2003 
robot_control_comfirmloc_req 
Confirm correct location 
2004 
robot_control_cancelreloc_req 
Cancel relocation 
2010 
robot_control_motion_req 
Open loop 
2022 
robot_control_loadmap_req 
Toggle loaded map 
… 
… 
… 
Response 
The response from the robot control API is returned to the client immediately and does not wait for the robot to complete. If 
ret_code does not exist, the command will be executed, but it does not mean that execution of the command has been completed. 
For some control commands, such as (2022) switch map, the state of loading map can be queried by (1022). Most of the other 
commands are instantaneous, and the customer doesn't need to care when the robot will finish, just know that the robot will run 
the command.

15.1.1.4.5 Cancel Relocation 
It is used to cancel the relocation process. If the relocation is currently being performed (that is, when reloc_status = 2), the 
relocation will be canceled, the position of the robot will return to the position before the relocation instruction is sent, and the 
reloc_status will equal to 3 (relocation success). If there is no relocation currently in progress, this command has no effect. 
Request 
• 
API number: 2004 (0x07D4) 
• 
Name: robot_control_cancelreloc_req 
• 
Description: Cancel relocation. 
• 
JSON data area: None 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 07 D4 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
• 
API number: 12004 (0x2EE4) 
• 
Name: robot_control_cancelreloc_res 
• 
Description: Response of cancelling relocation 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
ret_code 
Number 
API error code 
YES 
create_on 
String 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
String 
Error message 
YES 
Response Example 
{ 
  "ret_code": 0 
} 
 
15.1.1.4.6 Open Loop Motion 
Controls onlt through vx, vy,and w for multi-steering wheel. 
Request 
• 
API number: 2010 (0x07DA) 
• 
Name: robot_control_motion_req 
• 
Description: Open loop motion. 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
vx 
Number 
The speed of the robot in the x-axis direction in the robot coordinate system, default is 0, unit: m/s 
YES 
vy 
Number 
The speed of the robot in the y-axis direction in the robot coordinate system, default is 0, unit: m/s 
YES 
w 
Number 
The angular velocity of the robot in the robot coordinate system (i.e., turn clockwise to negative and 
counterclockwise to positive), default is 0, unit: rad/s 
YES 
steer 
number 
-2= back to zero, 1=15° increment, -1=15° decrement (robot coordinate system), and this value is valid 
only for the robots with a single steering wheel. When this field exists, it does not respond to vy and w, 
and vx indicates the line speed of the steering wheel. 
是 
real_steer 
number 
The target rudder angle value (robot coordinate system), unit: rad; This value is only valid for the robots 
with a single steering wheel. When this field exists, it does not respond to vy and w, and vx indicates the 
line speed of the steering wheel, but its priority is higher than steer. 
是 
duration 
Number 
The duration of the robot's open-loop speed movement, unit ms, 0 = keep the current open-loop speed 
movement, this parameter defaults to the value of ControlMotionDuration in the parameter 
configuration. 
YES 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 13 07 DA 00 00 00 00 00 00 
{"vx":0.5,"vy":0.5} 
// After serialization, the hex is: 
7B 22 76 78 22 3A 30 2E 35 2C 22 76 79 22 3A 30 2E 35 7D 
Response 
• 
API number: 12010 (0x2EEA) 
• 
Name: robot_control_motion_res 
• 
Description: Response of open loop motion 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default

Number

YES

String

String

15.1.1.5 Robot Navigation API 
The robot navigation API is mainly used to send navigation related commands. 
15.1.1.5.1 API List 
Request 
Note: All commands cannot be performed simultaneously. 
Response 
The robot navigation API will immediately respond to the client without waiting for the robot to perform navigation. If ret_code 
does not exist or is 0, it means that the navigation will be executed, but it does not mean that the navigation has been completed. 
API Number 
Name 
Description

Query a robot task list 
3106

Execute pre-stored tasklist 
… 
… 
… 
The user needs to query the status of the navigation through the robot status API (1020). A robot can only have one navigation at a 
time, and new navigation instructions will interrupt the previous navigation.

15.1.1.5.5 Path Navigation 
Path navigation is to send a target station to the robot who automatically plans the path to run, and passes through the 
intermediate station without stopping. 
Request 
• 
API number: 3051 (0x0BEB) 
• 
Name: robot_task_gotarget_req 
• 
Description: Path navigation 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
 
1. Fixed Path Navigation 
// Example 1.1 The robot goes to LM1 along the line LM2->LM1 
{ 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "id": "LM1", 
  "task_id": "87654321" 
} 
Fixed path navigation supports user-defined optional attributes. For example, it supports the configuration of parameters such as 
maximum speed, maximum acceleration, and angle of arrival. A complete fixed path navigation command is shown in example 1.2. 
// Example 1.2 fixed path navigation command 
{ 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "id": "LM1", 
  "task_id": "87654321", 
  "angle": 1.57, 
  "method": "backward", 
  "max_speed": 0.2, 
  "max_wspeed": 0.2, 
  "max_acc": 0.1, 
  "max_wacc": 0.1, 
  "duration": 100, 
  "orientation": 90, 
  "spin": true 
} 
:-: Table 1.1. Fixed Path Navigation Command 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
id 
string 
Target station name 
When the robot performs operation in place, its value is "SELF_POSITION" 
NO 
source_id 
string 
Source station name 
When the starting position is not on a station but the current position of the robot, its value is 
"SELF_POSITION" 
NO 
task_id 
string 
Task id 
NO 
angle 
number 
The angle of target station in world coordinate system, unit rad 
YES 
method 
string 
Movement method, can only be "forward" or "backward", if this value is default, the movement 
method will be set to the method configured on the path 
YES 
max_speed 
number 
Maximum speed, unit m/s 
YES

2. Fixed Path Navigation with PGV Secondary Location Adjustment 
After the robot reaches the target station, it can perform a secondary adjustment of its position based on the QR code on the 
ground or on the shelf. 
There are four ways to adjust PGV. For specific adjustment methods, see 
[https://shimo.im/docs/r16q8MwZOWos6k7D](https://shimo.im/docs/r16q8MwZOWos6k7D. Among them, you can only choose 
either pgv_x_adjust or pgv_adjust_dist or neither. 
// Example 2.1. From LM2 to AP1, the robot uses pgv to perform a secondary adjustment of its position. 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "123456", 
  "use_pgv": true,            //adjust position by using upview PGV 
  "pgv_adjust_dist": 0.3,    //maximum adjustment radius 
  "pgv_adjust_cx": -0.3,    //center offset of adjustment range 
  "pgv_adjust_cy": 0 
} 
:-: Table 2.1. Second Adjustment Command of Path Navigation Based on QR Code 
 
 
 
 
Field name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
default 
use_pgv 
bool 
Whether to use the upview PGV to identify the QR code for the secondary adjustment of the 
position 
YES, false by 
default 
pgv_adjust_dist 
number 
Maximum adjustment radius (used for the third and fourth adjustment methods) 
YES 
pgv_adjust_cx 
number 
The offset between x coordinate of the center point in secondary adjustment range 
and x coordinate of the center point in the QR code coordinate system (this coordinate system is 
parallel to the current robot coordinate system), (used for the fourth adjustment method) 
YES 
pgv_ajdust_cy 
number 
The offset between y coordinate of the center point in secondary adjustment range 
and y coordinate of the center point in the QR code coordinate system (this coordinate system is 
parallel to the current robot coordinate system), (used for the fourth adjustment method) 
YES 
pgv_x_adjust 
number 
In the PGV adjustment mode, only the error in the x direction of the car is adjusted (used for the 
second adjustment method) 
YES 
use_dow_pgv 
bool 
Whether to use the down PGV to identify the QR code for the secondary adjustment of the position 
YES 
 
3. Fixed Path Navigation with Operation 
The robot supports the control of jack equipment, fork equipment, spin equipment and hook equipment. 
 
3.1 Jacking 
The robot can jack up the goods or put the goods down through recognition. 
// Example 3.1.1. The robot reaches AP1 by identifying the shelf, and then uses the QR code on the shelf to perform 
secondary positioning, and then lift the goods up 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "JackLoad", 
  "recognize": true, 
  "use_pgv": true 
} 
// Example 3.1.2 The robot arrives at AP1, and then adjusts its position through the down PGV, and then puts down the 
goods 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "JackUnload", 
  "use_down_pgv": true 
} 
// Example 3.1.3. The robot reaches AP1 and raises the jack equipment to a height of 0.2m 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "JackHeight", 
  "jack_height": 0.2 
} 
:-: Table 3.1. Path navigation with jacking equipment 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
operation 
string 
Control the actions of jack equipment, supported actions 
JackLoad (Lift up and load cargo) 
JackUnload (Jack down) 
JackHeight (Jack up) 
Wait (No action) 
YES, default is Wait. 
jack_height 
number 
When operation equals to JackHeight, the height of jack 
YES 
 
3.2 Fork 
The robot (fork or hand hydraulic carrier) can lift up or put down the pallet through recognition. 
// Example 3.2.1. The robot moves the fork to the start_height height, and then determines the position of the target 
point by identifying the pallet, and then the robot moves to the target point, and then the robot lifts the shelf and 
loads the goods 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "ForkLoad", 
  "start_height": 0.1, 
  "end_height": 1.0, 
  "recognize": true 
} 
// Example 3.2.2. The robot moves the fork to start_height, then the robot moves to the target point, and then the robot 
lowers the fork and unloads the goods 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "ForkUnload", 
  "start_height": 0.5, 
  "end_height": 0.1 
} 
// Example 3.2.3. The robot raises the fork to a height of 0.5m on the way to AP1 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "ForkHeight", 
  "fork_mid_height": 0.5 
} 
// Example 3.2.4. The robot raises the fork to a height of 0.1m after going to AP1 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "ForkHeight", 
  "end_height": 0.1 
} 
// Example 3.2.5. The robot moves forward the fork to 0.1m after going to AP1 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "ForkForward", 
  "fork_dist": 0.1 
} 
// Example 3.2.6. The robot moves the fork to start_height and determines the target position by recognizing the pallet 
(shelf/ S0002. Shelf)   
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "operation": "ForkLoad", 
  "start_height": 0.1, 
  "end_height": 1.0, 
  "recognize": true, 
  "recfile":"shelf/s0002.shelf" 
}

3.6 Waiting for DI Trigger 
Example 3.5.1: After the robot reaches AP1 station, the robot waits for DI1 to become true and DI2 to false, or waits for 10s to 
complete the task. 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "operation": "WaitDI", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12345", 
  "args": { 
    "DI": [ 
      { 
        "id": 1, 
        "status": true 
      }, 
      { 
        "id": 2, 
        "status": false 
      } 
    ], 
    "timeout": 10 
  } 
} 
You also can use the following way, but this is not recommended. 
{ 
  "id": "AP1", 
  "operation": "WaitDI", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12345", 
  "1": true, 
  "2": false 
}

4. Performing "operation" in Place 
The operation of the robot not only can be executed before, during and after the path navigation, but also can be executed in 
place. In-place execution needs to set both id and source_id to "SELF_POSITION" 
// Example 4.1 shows the operation of JackLoad at the current place 
{ 
  "id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "source_id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "task_id": "12345678abcdefgh", 
  "operation": "JackLoad" 
}

5.1 Universal Script 
The robot can execute the script before, during, or after path navigation. 
// Example 5.1.1 shows that the robot **after** goes to the LM1, executes the script firstScript.py, the input parameter

  "script_stage": 2

the script is {"hello":"world"}.

  "script_name": "firstScript.py", 
  "script_args": { 
    "hello": "world" 
  }, 
  "operation": "Script", 
  "id": "LM1", 
  "source_id": "LM2", 
  "task_id": "12344321", 
  "script_stage": 1

of the script is {"hello":"world"}.

    "hello": "world"

5.2 Built-in Script goPath.py, Navigating by Custom Path 
The goPath.py is used to send a path in the world coordinate system or robot coordinate system to the robot. 
// Example 5.2.1 shows that the robot is at the current position, execute the script goPath.py, the input parameter of 
the script means that the robot walks 1m forward in its own coordinate system. 
{ 
  "script_name": "syspy/goPath.py", 
  "script_args": { 
    "x": 1.0, 
    "y": 0.0, 
    "coordinate": "robot" 
  }, 
  "operation": "Script", 
  "id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "source_id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "task_id": "12344321" 
} 
// Example 5.2.2 shows that the robot is at the current position, and the script goPath.py is executed. The incoming 
parameters of the script indicate that the robot walks to the position of x:1.0, y:0.0 in the world coordinate system. 
{ 
  "script_name": "syspy/goPath.py", 
  "script_args": { 
    "x": 1.0, 
    "y": 0.0, 
    "coordinate": "world" 
  }, 
  "operation": "Script", 
  "id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "source_id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "task_id": "12344321" 
} 
:-: Table 5.2.1 Description of goPath.py input parameters 
 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether default

double 
x coordinate, unit m 
NO 
y 
double 
y coordinate, unit m 
NO

string 
"robot"=robot coordinate system 
"world"=world coordinate system 
NO

YES

5.4 Built-in Script waitDI.py 
The waitDI.py script is used to make the car wait for certain DIs to reach a certain state, or reach a timeout condition, and then the 
task is completed 
// Example 5.4.1 shows that the robot is at the current position and executes the script waitDI.py. The input parameter 
of the script means that the robot plays wind audio, and then waits in place for DI1 to become true and DI2 to false, or 
waits for 10s to complete the task. The audio ends. 
{ 
  "script_name": "syspy/waitDI.py", 
  "script_args": { 
    "DI": [ 
      { 
        "id": 1, 
        "status": true 
      }, 
      { 
        "id": 2, 
        "status": false 
      } 
    ], 
    "timeout": 10, 
    "soundName": "wind" 
  }, 
  "operation": "Script", 
  "id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "source_id": "SELF_POSITION", 
  "task_id": "12344321" 
}

15.1.1.5.6 Path Navigation 2 
The path navigation is a given target station, which is automatically planned by the robot to run alon.g the Bezier curve path, 
during the path navigation robot will pass through other intermediate stations but will not stop. 
Request 
• 
API number: 3052 (0x0BEC) 
• 
Name: robot_task_gotarget2_req 
• 
Description: Path navigation 2 
• 
JSON data area: See below. 
Note 1: Angle is the arrival direction of the robot, and the value set on the station will be used by default. 
 
Note 2: The max_speed, max_wspeed, max_acc, max_wacc fields are not recommended. It is better to control these values through 
the path and area attributes or robot parameters on the map, and these fields may be deleted in the future.

{"id":"LM2"} 
// go to LM2 
// The hexadecimal after serialization is:

// go to LM10

{"id":"LM102"} 
// go to LM102 
// The hexadecimal after serialization is: 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 0E 0B EC 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 69 64 22 3A 22 4C 4D 31 30 32 22 7D 
Operation Description When navigating to an AP (or TL, WL) station using path navigation in Roboshop, you can choose to execute 
an action (meaning navigating to the AP and executing the action), as shown in the figure below: 
 
 Various actions can be 
performed according to the execution object and recognition model file configured on the AP point 
 At this time, more 
parameters need to be added to the path navigation commands to make the robot navigate to the target station and complete the 
corresponding actions. Thecommands are as follows: 
1. Fork The execution object of the AP station needs to be configured as fork, and the recognition model file is configured as a 
pallet model file or not configured as required. operation: action can be "ForkLoad" or "ForkUnload" recognize: Indicates 
whether recognition is required when inserting the pallet (if recognition is required, please ensure that the recognition model 
file is configured correctly) layer: The number of pallet layers that need to be inserted into the fork (only meaningful when 
recognize = true) start_height: When the action starts, the starting height of the fork (only meaningful when recognize = 
false) end_height: After the action is over, the end height of the fork (only meaningful when recognize = false) 
2. An example of sending data area is as follows: 
3. // recognize = false 
4. { 
5. "id": "AP1", 
6. "operation": "ForkLoad", 
7. "layer": 0, 
8. "recognize": true 
9. } 
10. // recognize = true 
11. { 
12. "id": "AP1", 
13. "operation": "ForkUnload", 
14. "start_height": 1.0, 
15. "end_height": 0, 
16. "recognize": false 
} 
17. Roller The execution object of the AP station needs to be configured as roller, and the recognition model file does not need 
to be configured (the roller does not currently have recognition). operation: action can be "RollerLoad" or 
"RollerUnload" direction: directions of action for roller, can be "left" or "right" recognize: Whether need to recognition or 
not (For roller, recognition is currently invalid) 
18. An example of sending data area is as follows: 
19. { 
20. "id": "AP1", 
21. "operation": "RollerLoad", 
22. "direction ": "left", 
23. "recognize": false    // You can also omit the recognize field 
} 
24. Jack The execution object of the AP station needs to be configured as jack, and the recognition model file is configured as a 
shelf model file or not configured as required operation: action can be "JackLoad" or "JackUnload" or 
"JackHeight" jack_height: set height for jack (only meaningful when operation = "JackHeight") recognize: Represents 
whether recognition is required when drilling into the shelf (if recognition is required, please ensure that the recognition 
model file is configured correctly, for the use of recognition the shelf while drilling, please refer to this tutorial) use_pgv: 
represents whether the PGV sensor is used to correct the position after drilling into the shelf 
25. An example of sending data area is as follows: 
26. { 
27. "id": "AP1", 
28. "operation": "JackLoad",    // jack up 
29. "recognize": false, 
30. "use_pgv": false 
31. } 
32. or 
33. { 
34. "id": "AP1", 
35. "operation": "JackUnload",    // jack down 
36. "recognize": false, 
37. "use_pgv": false 
38. } 
39. or 
40. { 
41. "id": "AP1", 
42. "operation": "JackHeight",    // set fixed height to jack 
43. "jack_height": 0.2, 
44. "recognize": false, 
45. "use_pgv": false 
} 
46. Hook The execution object of the AP station needs to be configured as hook, and the recognition model file is configured as 
the material truck model file or not configured as required. operation: actoin can be "HookLoad" or 
"HookUnload" recognize: represents whether it needs to be recognized before hooking the material truck 
47. An example of sending data area is as follows: 
48. { 
49. "id": "AP1", 
50. "operation": "HookLoad",    // hook load 
51. "recognize": false 
52. } 
53. or 
54. { 
55. "id": "AP1", 
56. "operation": "HookUnload",    // hook down 
57. "recognize": false 
} 
 
Response 
• 
API number: 13052 (0x32FC) 
• 
Name: robot_task_gotarget2_res 
• 
Description: Response of path navigation 2 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
ret_code 
number 
API error code 
YES 
create_on 
string 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
string 
error message 
YES 
Response Example 
{ 
  "ret_code": 0 
} 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 0E 32 FC 0B EC 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 72 65 74 5F 63 6F 64 65 22 3A 30 7D

15.1.1.5.8 Translation 
Request 
• 
API number: 3055 (0x0BEF) 
• 
Name: robot_task_translate_req 
• 
Description: Translation; Move a fixed distance in a straight line at a fixed speed. 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Note: 3055(Translation), 3056(Rotation), 3057 cannot be performed simultaneously 
 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
dist 
number 
Linear movement distance, absolute value, unit: m 
NO 
vx 
number 
The movement speed for X direction in the robot coordinate system, positive is forward, negative is 
backward, unit: m/s 
YES 
vy 
number 
The movement speed for Y direction in the robot coordinate system, positive is to the left, negative 
is to the right, unit: m/s 
YES 
mode 
number 
0 = mileage mode (Motion based on mileage), 1 = localization mode, default is mileage mode 
YES 
If vx and vy both have values, then will use composition of velocities. Mileage mode does not require precise localization, but it may 
produce large errors for long-distance movements. The error increases with distance. The localization mode requires stable 
localization in the current environment, and the error is related to the current environment and localization accuracy. 
Request Example 
{"dist":5.0,"vx":0.5,"vy":0.5} 
// move straight for 5m 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 1E 0B EF 00 00 00 00 00 00  
7B 22 64 69 73 74 22 3A 35 2E 30 2C 22 76 78 22  
3A 30 2E 35 2C 22 76 79 22 3A 30 2E 35 7D 
Response 
• 
API number: 13055 (0x32FF) 
• 
Name: robot_task_translate_res 
• 
Description: Response of translation 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
ret_code 
number 
API error code 
YES 
create_on 
string 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
string 
error message 
YES 
Response Example 
{ 
  "ret_code": 0 
} 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 0E 32 FF 0B EF 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 72 65 74 5F 63 6F 64 65 22 3A 30 7D 
 
 
15.1.1.5.9 Rotation 
Request 
• 
API number: 3056 (0x0BF0) 
• 
Name: robot_task_turn_req 
• 
Description: Rotation, rotate a fixed angle at a fixed angular speed 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Note: 3055(Translation), 3056(Rotation), 3057 cannot be performed simultaneously 
Field 
Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
angle 
number 
Rotation angle (robot coordinate system), absolute value, unit: rad, can be greater than 2π 
NO 
vw 
number 
Angular speed of rotation (robot coordinate system), positive for counterclockwise rotation, negative 
for clockwise rotation, unit: rad/s 
NO 
mode 
number 
0 = mileage mode (Motion based on mileage), 1 = localization mode, default is mileage mode 
YES 
The mileage mode does not require precise localization, but for a large rotation angle, a large error may occur, and the error 
increases as the rotation angle increases. The localization mode requires stable localization in the current environment, and the 
error is related to the current environment and localization accuracy. 
Request Example 
{"angle":3.14,"vw":1.6} 
// rotate 3.14 rad with rotation speed 1.6rad/s 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 17 0B F0 00 00 00 00 00 00  
7B 22 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 33 2E 31 34 2C 22 76  
77 22 3A 31 2E 36 7D

15.1.1.5.10 Pallet Rotation 
Request 
• 
API number: 3057 (0x0BF1) 
• 
Name: robot_task_spin_req 
• 
Description: Tray rotation 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Note 1: 3055(Translation), 3056(Rotation), 3057 cannot be performed simultaneously 
 
Note 2: All angles of tray rotation are in "radians" 
 
Note 3: When the tray is not in following mode, if the jack is in the down state, the robot will automatically reset the tray angle to 
zero before navigating. If the jack is in the up state, the robot will automatically reset the tray angle to zero or turn to 180 degrees 
before navigating. This feature can be turned off by setting the parameters AutoSpinToZeroInUnload (down state) and 
AutoSpinToZero (up state) to false. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether 
Default 
increase_spin_angle 
number 
Add an angle to the current tray angle. If the angle is positive, rotate counterclockwise, and if 
it is negative, rotate clockwise, unit: rad 
YES 
robot_spin_angle 
number 
Rotate the angle of the tray to an angle under the robot coordinate system. spin_direction is 0, 
then turn to the nearest; spin_direction is 1, then turn counterclockwise; spin_direction is -1, 
then turn clockwise, unit: rad 
YES 
global_spin_angle 
number 
Rotate the angle of the tray to an angle in the world coordinate system. spin_direction is 0, 
then turn to the nearest; spin_direction is 1, then turn counterclockwise; spin_direction is -1, 
then turn clockwise 
YES 
spin_direction 
number 
0 = nearest, 1 = counterclockwise -1 = clockwise 
YES 
Request Example 
{"increase_spin_angle":1.57} 
//  Rotate 1.57 radians counterclockwise 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 0B F1 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 69 6E 63 72 65 61 73 65 5F 73 70 69 6E 5F 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 31 2E 35 37 7D 
{"robot_spin_angle":-1.57,"spin_direction":0.0} 
//  Turn nearest to -1.57 radians (robot coordinate system) 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 0B F1 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 72 6F 62 6F 74 5F 73 70 69 6E 5F 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 2D 31 2E 35 37 2C 22 73 70 69 6E 5F 64 69 72 65 63 74 69 6F 
6E 22 3A 30 2E 30 7D 
{"global_spin_angle":-1.57,"spin_direction":0.0} 
//  Turn nearest to -1.57 radians (world coordinate system) 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 0B F1 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 67 6C 6F 62 61 6C 5F 73 70 69 6E 5F 61 6E 67 6C 65 22 3A 2D 31 2E 35 37 2C 22 73 70 69 6E 5F 64 69 72 65 63 74 69 
6F 6E 22 3A 30 2E 30 7D 
Response 
• 
API number: 13057 (0x3301)

string

15.1.1.5.12 Designated Path Navigation 
The designated path navigation is to send a set of station sequences to the robot. The robot will navigate according to this 
sequence (no longer autonomously plan the route), and will not stop when pass through the intermediate station. 
 
Robokit 3.3 and above version must contain three parameters: "source_id" represents the starting point of the path, "id" represents 
the end of the path, and "task_id" represents the unique number of the task. 
 
The sequence of stations in the specified path must be continuous stations in the map. There must be no gaps between the 
stations, nor can it contain disconnected stations, otherwise the robot will report an error. 
Request 
• 
API number: 3066 (0x0BFA) 
• 
Name: robot_task_gotargetlist_req 
• 
Description: Designated path navigation 
• 
JSON data area: See below 
Refer to Path Navigation 3051, where task_id, id, and source_id are required fields and cannot be omitted. 
Request Example 
// path: LM1 -> LM2 -> AP1 (then execute JackHeight) 
{ 
  "move_task_list": [ 
    { 
      "id": "LM2", 
      "source_id": "LM1", 
      "task_id": "12344321" 
    }, 
    { 
      "id": "AP1", 
      "source_id": "LM2", 
      "task_id": "12344322", 
      "operation": "JackHeight", 
      "jack_height": 0.2 
    } 
  ] 
} 
// path: LM1 -> LM2 -> AP1 (then execute JackHeight) 
{ 
  "move_task_list": [ 
    { 
      "id": "LM2" 
    }, 
    { 
      "id": "AP1", 
      "operation": "JackHeight", 
      "jack_height": 0.2 
    } 
  ] 
} 
Response 
• 
API number: 13066 (0x330A) 
• 
Name: robot_task_gotargetlist_res 
• 
Description: Response of designated path navigation 
• 
JSON data area: See table below 
 
 
 
 
Response Example 
{ 
  "ret_code": 0 
} 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 0E 33 0A 0B FA 00 00 00 00  
7B 22 72 65 74 5F 63 6F 64 65 22 3A 30 7D

Release Control 
Releases control to the dispatching system, and it can only be enabled when the location status is success. When the control is 
successfully released to the dispatch system, the robot will not respond to any commands except status query. 
After the control is released, any navigation in progress currently will be canceled. 
Request 
• 
API number: 4002 (0x0FA2) 
• 
Name: robot_config_release_req 
• 
Description: Release control 
• 
JSON data area: None 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 00 0F A2 00 00 00 00 00 00 
Response 
• 
API number: 14002 (0x36B2) 
•

Release Control 
You can only release the control that you have preempted, and you cannot release the control of others. If you want to gain control, 
you must preempt it. 
Request 
• 
API number: 4006 (0x0FA6) 
• 
Name: robot_config_unlock_req 
• 
Description: Release control. 
• 
JSON data area: None

Add Dynamic Obstacles (Robot Coordinate System) 
Request 
• 
API number: 4350 (0x10FE) 
• 
Name: robot_config_addobstacle_req 
• 
Description: Add dynamic obstacles (robot coordinate system). 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Add a rectangular dynamic obstacle in the robot coordinate system. 
Field name 
Type 
Description 
name 
string 
Obstacle name, unique 
x1 
double 
The x coordinate of the first vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
y1 
double 
The y coordinate of the first vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
x2 
double 
The x coordinate of the second vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
y2 
double 
The y coordinate of the second vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
x3 
double 
The x coordinate of the third vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
y3 
double 
The y coordinate of the third vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
x4 
double 
The x coordinate of the fourth vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
y4 
double 
The y coordinate of the fourth vertex of the rectangle (robot coordinate system), unit m 
Request Example 
{"name":"obstacle2","x1":2.0,"y1":0.6,"x2":4.0,"y2":0.6,"x3":4.0,"y3":1.2,"x4":2.0,"y4":1.2} 
// Add dynamic obstacle2 in robot coordinate system. 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 5C 10 FE 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 6E 61 6D 65 22 3A 22 6F 62 73 74 61 63 6C  
65 32 22 2C 22 78 31 22 3A 32 2E 30 2C 22 79 31  
22 3A 30 2E 36 2C 22 78 32 22 3A 34 2E 30 2C 22  
79 32 22 3A 30 2E 36 2C 22 78 33 22 3A 34 2E 30  
2C 22 79 33 22 3A 31 2E 32 2C 22 78 34 22 3A 32  
2E 30 2C 22 79 34 22 3A 31 2E 32 7D 
When the server receives the detailed coordinates of the dynamic obstacle, it will add the obstacle to the corresponding 
coordinates in the robot coordinate system. 
As shown in the following figure:

Set Third-Party Error 
After setting, an error code of 52900 will be generated, the robot stops moving, and Roboshop can see the following alarm: "an 
error" refers to the content passed in msg. 
 
Request 
• 
API number: 4800 (0x12C0) 
• 
Name: robot_config_seterror_req 
• 
Description: Set third-party error. 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
msg 
string 
Description of Error, English only 
NO 
Request Example 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 2E 12 C0 00 00 00 00 00 00 
{"msg":"an error from netprotocol tcp/ip api"} 
// The hexadecimal after serialization is: 
7B 22 6D 73 67 22 3A 22 61 6E 20 65 72 72 6F 72  
20 66 72 6F 6D 20 6E 65 74 70 72 6F 74 6F 63 6F  
6C 20 74 63 70 2F 69 70 20 61 70 69 22 7D 
Response 
• 
API number: 14800 (0x39D0) 
• 
Name: robot_config_seterror_res 
• 
Description: Response of setting third-party error. 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default

Number 
API error code 
YES

String 
API upload timestamp 
YES 
err_msg 
String 
Error message 
YES

  "ret_code": 0

7B 22 72 65 74 5F 63 6F 64 65 22 3A 30 7D

Configure Robot Push Port 
Request 
• 
API number: 4091 (0x0FFB) 
• 
Name: robot_config_push_req 
• 
Description: Configure robot push port 19301. 
• 
JSON data area: See table below. 
Field Name 
Type 
Description 
Whether Default 
interval 
Interger 
Message push interval (ms) 
YES 
included_fields 
Array[string] 
Set the fields included in the message. 
YES 
excluded_fields 
Array[string] 
Set excluded fields in messages. 
YES 
include_fields and exclude_fields cannot be set at the same time 
Request Example 
// Set interval and include_fields at the same time. 
{"interval":2000,"included_fields":["vx","vy"]} 
5A 01 00 01 00 00 00 2F 0F FB 00 00 00 00 00 00 
7B 22 69 6E 74 65 72 76 61 6C 22 3A 32 30 30 30  
2C 22 69 6E 63 6C 75 64 65 64 5F 66 69 65 6C 64  
73 22 3A 5B 22 76 78 22 2C 22 76 79 22 5D 7D 
Response 
• 
API number: 14091 (0x370B) 
• 
Name: robot_config_push_res 
• 
Description: Response of configuring robot push port 
• 
JSON data area: See table below 
Field name 
Type 
Description 
Whether default 
ret_code 
Number 
API error code 
YES

String 
API upload timestamp 
YES

String 
Error message 
YES

  "ret_code": 0
